</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;padding-top:0.15em;">
<img alt="Category" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/16px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png" title="Category" width="16" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/24px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/32px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="36" data-file-height="31" /> <a href="/wiki/Category:Antisemitism" title="Category:Antisemitism">Category</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Antisemitism" title="Template:Antisemitism"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Antisemitism" title="Template talk:Antisemitism"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Antisemitism&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Holocaust denial</b> is the act of denying the <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-definition_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-definition-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust deniers claim that <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a> was aimed only at <a href="/wiki/Expulsions_and_exoduses_of_Jews" title="Expulsions and exoduses of Jews">deporting Jews</a> from the Reich but that it did not include the extermination of Jews; that Nazi authorities did not use <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber" title="Gas chamber">gas chambers</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murder</a> Jews; or that the actual number of Jews killed was significantly lower than the historically accepted figure of 5 to 6 million, typically around a tenth of that figure.<sup id="cite_ref-often_claims_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-often_claims-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Key_elements_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Key_elements-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Because Holocaust denial is a common facet of certain racist propaganda, it is considered a serious societal problem in many places where it occurs and is <a href="/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial" title="Laws against Holocaust denial">illegal in several European countries and Israel</a>. 
</p><p>In some post-Soviet states, Holocaust deniers do not deny the very fact of mass murder of Jews, but they deny some national or regional elements of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Scholars use the term <i><a href="/wiki/Denialism" title="Denialism">denial</a></i> to describe the views and methodology of Holocaust deniers in order to distinguish them from legitimate <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism" title="Historical revisionism">historical revisionists</a>, who challenge orthodox interpretations of history using established historical <a href="/wiki/Methodology" title="Methodology">methodologies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-terminology_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terminology-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust deniers generally do not accept <i>denial</i> as an appropriate description of their activities and use the euphemism <i><a href="/wiki/Historical_negationism" title="Historical negationism">revisionism</a></i> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-Revisionist_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revisionist-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The methodologies of Holocaust deniers are often based on a predetermined conclusion that ignores overwhelming historical evidence to the contrary.<sup id="cite_ref-predetermined_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-predetermined-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most Holocaust deniers claim, either explicitly or implicitly, that the Holocaust is a hoax—or at best an exaggeration—arising from a deliberate <a href="/wiki/Jewish_conspiracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish conspiracy">Jewish conspiracy</a> designed to advance the interest of Jews at the expense of other people.<sup id="cite_ref-hoax_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoax-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> For this reason, Holocaust denial is generally considered to be an <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">antisemitic</a><sup id="cite_ref-antisemitic_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antisemitic-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-conspiracy_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conspiracy-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Terminology_and_etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Terminology and etymology</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Background"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Background</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Efforts_to_conceal_the_historical_record"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Efforts to conceal the historical record</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology_and_etymology">Terminology and etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology and etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Holocaust deniers prefer to refer to their work as historical revisionism, and object to being referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Denialism" title="Denialism">deniers</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Revisionist_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revisionist-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a> has written that: "The deniers' selection of the name revisionist to describe themselves is indicative of their basic strategy of deceit and distortion and of their attempt to portray themselves as legitimate historians engaged in the traditional practice of illuminating the past."<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Scholars consider this misleading since the methods of Holocaust denial differ from those of legitimate historical revision.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Legitimate historical revisionism is explained in a resolution adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a> History Department, November 8, 1991, and reprinted in <i>Duke Chronicle</i>, November 13, 1991 in response to an advertisement produced by Bradley R Smith's <a href="/wiki/CODOH" class="mw-redirect" title="CODOH">Committee for Open Debate on the Holocaust</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>That historians are constantly engaged in historical revision is certainly correct; however, what historians do is very different from this advertisement. Historical revision of major events ... is not concerned with the actuality of these events; rather, it concerns their historical interpretation – their causes and consequences generally.
</p></blockquote>
<p>Lipstadt writes that modern Holocaust denial draws its inspiration from various sources, including a school of thought which used an established method to question government policies.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992 Donald L. Niewyk gave some examples of how legitimate historical revisionism—the re-examination of accepted history and its updating with newly discovered, more accurate, or less-biased information—may be applied to the study of the Holocaust as new facts emerge to change the historical understanding of it:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>With the main features of the Holocaust clearly visible to all but the willfully blind, historians have turned their attention to aspects of the story for which the evidence is incomplete or ambiguous. These are not minor matters by any means, but turn on such issues as Hitler's role in the event, Jewish responses to persecution, and reactions by onlookers both inside and outside Nazi-controlled Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In contrast, the Holocaust denial movement bases its approach on the predetermined idea that the Holocaust, as understood by mainstream historiography, did not occur.<sup id="cite_ref-predetermined_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-predetermined-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Sometimes referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Historical_negationism" title="Historical negationism">negationism</a>", from the French term <i>négationnisme</i> introduced by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rousso" title="Henry Rousso">Henry Rousso</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust deniers attempt to rewrite history by minimizing, denying or simply ignoring essential facts. <a href="/wiki/Koenraad_Elst" title="Koenraad Elst">Koenraad Elst</a> writes:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Negationism means the denial of historical crimes against humanity. It is not a reinterpretation of known facts, but the denial of known facts. The term negationism has gained currency as the name of a movement to deny a specific crime against humanity, the Nazi genocide on the Jews in 1941–45, also known as the Holocaust (Greek: complete burning) or the <i>Shoah</i> (Hebrew: disaster). Negationism is mostly identified with the effort at re-writing history in such a way that the fact of the Holocaust is omitted.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Efforts_to_conceal_the_historical_record">Efforts to conceal the historical record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Efforts to conceal the historical record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sonderaktion_1005" title="Sonderaktion 1005">Sonderaktion 1005</a> and <a href="/wiki/Posen_speeches" title="Posen speeches">Posen speeches</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png/220px-Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png/330px-Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png/440px-Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Members_of_a_Sonderkommando_1005_unit_pose_next_to_a_bone_crushing_machine_in_the_Janowska_concentration_camp.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of a <a href="/wiki/Sonderaktion_1005" title="Sonderaktion 1005">Sonderkommando 1005</a> unit pose next to a bone-crushing machine in the <a href="/wiki/Janowska_concentration_camp" title="Janowska concentration camp">Janowska concentration camp</a> in German-occupied Poland (Jun 1943&#160;– Oct 1943)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg/220px-Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg/330px-Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg/440px-Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohrdruf_Corpses_Eisenhower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>April 12, 1945: Generals <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Eisenhower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Bradley" title="Omar Bradley">Omar Bradley</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a> inspect, at <a href="/wiki/Ohrdruf_forced_labor_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohrdruf forced labor camp">Ohrdruf forced labor camp</a>, an improvised crematory pyre</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="German_efforts">German efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>While the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> was still underway, the Nazis had already formed a contingency plan that in case of defeat they would carry out the total destruction of German records.<sup id="cite_ref-klars-coth_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klars-coth-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historians have documented evidence that as Germany's defeat became imminent and Nazi leaders realized they would most likely be captured and brought to trial, great effort was made to destroy all evidence of mass extermination. <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> instructed his camp commandants to destroy records, crematoria, and other signs of mass extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-Arad_1984_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arad_1984-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As one of many examples, the bodies of the 25,000 mostly Latvian Jews whom <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Jeckeln" title="Friedrich Jeckeln">Friedrich Jeckeln</a> and the soldiers under his command had shot at <a href="/wiki/Rumbula_massacre" title="Rumbula massacre">Rumbula</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a>) in late 1941 were dug up and burned in 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-Ezer_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ezer-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Similar operations were undertaken at <a href="/wiki/Belzec_extermination_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Belzec extermination camp">Belzec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a> and other death camps.<sup id="cite_ref-Arad_1984_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arad_1984-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In the infamous <a href="/wiki/Posen_speeches" title="Posen speeches">Posen speeches</a> of October 1943 such as the one on October 4, Himmler explicitly referred to the extermination of the Jews of Europe and further stated that the genocide must be permanently kept, secret:<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Himmler-1943-Posen_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Himmler-1943-Posen-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I also want to refer here very frankly to a very difficult matter. We can now very openly talk about this among ourselves, and yet we will never discuss this publicly. Just as we did not hesitate <a href="/wiki/Night_of_the_Long_Knives" title="Night of the Long Knives">on June 30, 1934</a>, to perform our duty as ordered and put comrades who had failed up against the wall and execute them, we also never spoke about it, nor will we ever speak about it. Let us thank God that we had within us enough self-evident fortitude never to discuss it among us, and we never talked about it. Every one of us was horrified, and yet every one clearly understood that we would do it next time, when the order is given and when it becomes necessary.
I am now referring to the evacuation of the Jews, to the extermination of the Jewish people. </p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Heinrich Himmler, October 4, 1943</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="French_collaboration_in_archive_destruction">French collaboration in archive destruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French collaboration in archive destruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/German_military_administration_in_occupied_France_during_World_War_II" title="German military administration in occupied France during World War II">occupied France</a>, the situation with respect to preserving war records was not much better, partly as a result of French state secrecy rules dating back to well before the war aimed at protecting the French government and the state from embarrassing revelations, and partly to avoid culpability.   For example, at <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Paris" title="Liberation of Paris">Liberation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prefecture_of_Police" title="Prefecture of Police">Prefecture of Police</a> destroyed nearly all of the massive archive of Jewish arrest and deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-klars-coth_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klars-coth-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Efforts_to_preserve_the_historical_record">Efforts to preserve the historical record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Efforts to preserve the historical record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="During_the_war">During the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: During the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>One of the earliest efforts to save historical record of the Holocaust occurred during the war, in France, where <a href="/wiki/Drancy_internment_camp" title="Drancy internment camp">Drancy internment camp</a> records were carefully preserved and turned over to the new <a href="/w/index.php?title=French_Bureau_of_Veterans_and_War_Victims&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="French Bureau of Veterans and War Victims (page does not exist)">French Bureau of Veterans and War Victims</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/ONAC" class="extiw" title="fr:ONAC">fr</a>&#93;</sup>; however, the bureau then held them in secret, refusing to release copies later, even to the <a href="/wiki/Center_of_Contemporary_Jewish_Documentation" title="Center of Contemporary Jewish Documentation">Center of Contemporary Jewish Documentation</a> (CDJC).
</p><p>In 1943, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Schneersohn" title="Isaac Schneersohn">Isaac Schneersohn</a>, anticipating the need for a center to document and preserve the memory of the persecution for historical reasons and also support claims post-war, gathered together 40 representatives from Jewish organizations in <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a> which was under Italian occupation at the time<sup id="cite_ref-mdlShoah_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdlShoah-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> in order to form a <i>centre de documentation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jockusch_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jockusch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  Exposure meant the death penalty, and as a result little actually happened before <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberation of France">liberation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ej-cdjc_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ej-cdjc-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Serious work began after the center moved to Paris in late 1944 and was renamed the CDJC.<sup id="cite_ref-Jockusch_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jockusch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ej-cdjc_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ej-cdjc-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Immediate_post-war_period">Immediate post-war period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Immediate post-war period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1945, General Dwight D. Eisenhower, Supreme Allied Commander, anticipated that someday an attempt would be made to recharacterize the documentation of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi crimes">Nazi crimes</a> as propaganda and took steps against it:<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The same day<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> I saw my first horror camp. It was near the town of <a href="/wiki/Gotha" title="Gotha">Gotha</a>. I have never been able to describe my emotional reactions when I first came face to face with indisputable evidence of Nazi brutality and ruthless disregard of every shred of decency. Up to that time I had known about it only generally or through secondary sources. I am certain, however, that I have never at any time experienced an equal sense of shock.<br />
</p><p>I visited every nook and cranny of the camp because I felt it my duty to be in a position from then on to testify at first hand about these things in case there ever grew up at home the belief or assumption that "the stories of Nazi brutality were just propaganda". Some members of the visiting party were unable to go through with the ordeal. I not only did so but as soon as I returned to <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">Patton</a>'s headquarters that evening I sent communications to both Washington and London, urging the two governments to send instantly to Germany a random group of newspaper editors and representative groups from the national legislatures. I felt that the evidence should be immediately placed before the American and the British public in a fashion that would leave no room for cynical doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Eisenhower, upon finding the victims of the death camps, ordered all possible photographs to be taken, and for the German people from surrounding villages to be ushered through the camps and even made to bury the dead. He wrote the following to General <a href="/wiki/George_Marshall" title="George Marshall">George Marshall</a> after visiting a German internment camp near Gotha, Germany:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The visual evidence and the verbal testimony of starvation, cruelty, and bestiality were so overpowering as to leave me a bit sick. In one room, where they [there] were piled up twenty or thirty naked men, killed by starvation, George Patton would not even enter. He said that he would get sick if he did so. I made the visit deliberately, in order to be in a position to give first-hand evidence of these things if ever, in the future, there develops a tendency to charge these allegations merely to "propaganda".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuremberg_trials">Nuremberg trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nuremberg trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a> took place in Germany after the war in 1945–1946. The stated aim was to dispense justice in retribution for atrocities of the German government.  This Allied intention to administer justice post-war was first announced in 1943 in the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Declaration" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Declaration">Declaration on German Atrocities in Occupied Europe</a> and reiterated at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> and at Berlin in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright-1946_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright-1946-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  While the intention was not specifically to preserve the historical record of the Holocaust, some of the core documents required to prosecute the cases were provided to them by the <a href="/wiki/CDJC" class="mw-redirect" title="CDJC">CDJC</a>, and much of the huge trove of archives were then transferred to the CDJC after the trials and became the core of future Holocaust historiography.<sup id="cite_ref-Bensoussan_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bensoussan-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nuremberg trials were important historically, but the events were still very recent, television was in its infancy and not present, and there was a little public impact.  There were isolated moments of limited public awareness from Hollywood films such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diary_of_Anne_Frank" class="mw-redirect" title="The Diary of Anne Frank">The Diary of Anne Frank</a></i> (1959) or the 1961 <i><a href="/wiki/Judgment_at_Nuremberg" title="Judgment at Nuremberg">Judgment at Nuremberg</a></i> which had some newsreel footage of actual scenes from liberated Nazi concentration camps including scenes of piles of naked corpses laid out in rows and bulldozed into large pits, which was considered exceptionally graphic for the time.
Public awareness changed when the Eichmann trial riveted the world's attention fifteen years after Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-yadvashem-impact_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yadvashem-impact-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shandler-1999a_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shandler-1999a-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trial_of_Adolf_Eichmann">Trial of Adolf Eichmann</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Trial of Adolf Eichmann">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1961, the Israeli government captured <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Adolf Eichmann</a> in Argentina and brought him to Israel to stand trial for war crimes.
Chief prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Gideon_Hausner" title="Gideon Hausner">Gideon Hausner</a>'s intentions were not only to demonstrate Eichmann's guilt personally but to present material about the entire Holocaust, thus producing a comprehensive record.<sup id="cite_ref-Cesarani-2005_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cesarani-2005-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Israeli government arranged for the trial to have prominent media coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-Birn-2011_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birn-2011-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
Many major newspapers from all over the globe sent reporters and published front-page coverage of the story.<sup id="cite_ref-Cesarani-2005_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cesarani-2005-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
Israelis had the opportunity to watch live television broadcasts of the proceedings, and videotape was flown daily to the United States for broadcast the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-Cesarani-2005_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cesarani-2005-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shandler-1999b_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shandler-1999b-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II_history">Post-World War II history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-World War II history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Holocaust_deniers" title="Category:Holocaust deniers">Category:Holocaust deniers</a>.</div>
<p>In the immediate aftermath of the war, prior to the extensive documentation efforts by the allied forces, a sense of disbelief caused many to deny the initial reports of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FoguKansteiner2016_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoguKansteiner2016-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Compounding this disbelief was the memory of <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">forged newspaper accounts</a> of the <a href="/wiki/German_Corpse_Factory" title="German Corpse Factory">German Corpse Factory</a>, an anti-German <a href="/wiki/Atrocity_propaganda" title="Atrocity propaganda">atrocity propaganda</a> campaign during WWI, which was widely known to be false by 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_fake_news_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_fake_news-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1930s, the Nazi government used this propaganda against the British, claiming allegations of concentration camps were malicious lies put forward by the British government, and historians Joachim Neander and <a href="/wiki/Randal_Marlin" title="Randal Marlin">Randal Marlin</a> note that this story "encouraged later disbelief when early reports circulated about the Holocaust under Hitler".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_fake_news_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_fake_news-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victor_Cavendish-Bentinck" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Cavendish-Bentinck">Victor Cavendish-Bentinck</a>, chairman of the British Joint Intelligence Committee, noted that these reports were similar to "stories of employment of human corpses during the last war for the manufacture of fat which was a grotesque lie"; likewise, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Century" title="The Christian Century">The Christian Century</a></i> commented that "The parallel between this story and the 'corpse factory' atrocity tale of the First World War is too striking to be overlooked."<sup id="cite_ref-bgd_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgd-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Neander notes that "There can be no doubt that the reported commercial use of the corpses of the murdered Jews undermined the credibility of the news coming from Poland and delayed action that might have rescued many Jewish lives."<sup id="cite_ref-bgd_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgd-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">Neo-Nazi</a> movement has been revitalized by Holocaust denial. Small but vocal numbers of Neo-Nazis realized that recreation of a Hitlerite-style regime may be impossible, but a replica might be produced in the future and realized that to rehabilitate Nazism required the discrediting of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-Atkins_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atkins-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Elmer_Barnes">Harry Elmer Barnes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Harry Elmer Barnes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Harry_Elmer_Barnes" title="Harry Elmer Barnes">Harry Elmer Barnes</a>, at one time a mainstream American historian, assumed a Holocaust-denial stance in his later years. Between <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Barnes was an <a href="/wiki/Anti-war_movement" title="Anti-war movement">anti-war</a> writer and a leader of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism" title="Historical revisionism">historical revisionism</a> movement. Starting in 1924, Barnes worked closely with the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_the_Study_of_the_Causes_of_the_War" title="Centre for the Study of the Causes of the War">Centre for the Study of the Causes of the War</a>, a German government-funded think tank whose sole purpose was to disseminate the official government position that Germany was the victim of Allied aggression in 1914 and that the <a href="/wiki/Versailles_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Versailles Treaty">Versailles Treaty</a> was morally invalid.<sup id="cite_ref-Herwig_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herwig-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Headed by Major Alfred von Wegerer, a <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch_movement" title="Völkisch movement"><i>völkisch</i></a> activist, the organization portrayed itself as a scholarly society, but historians later described it as "a clearinghouse for officially desirable views on the outbreak of the war."<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following World War II, Barnes became convinced that allegations made against <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>, including the Holocaust, were wartime propaganda which had been used to justify the United States' involvement in World War II. Barnes claimed that there were two false claims made about World War II, namely that Germany started the war in 1939, and the Holocaust, which Barnes claimed did not happen.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_75_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_75-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his 1962 pamphlet, <i>Revisionism and Brainwashing</i>, Barnes claimed that there was a "lack of any serious opposition or concerted challenge to the atrocity stories and other modes of defamation of German national character and conduct".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Barnes argued that there was "a failure to point out the atrocities of the Allies were more brutal, painful, mortal and numerous than the most extreme allegations made against the Germans".<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He claimed that in order to justify the "horrors and evils of the Second World War", the Allies made the Nazis the "scapegoat" for their own misdeeds.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_75_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_75-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Barnes cited the French Holocaust denier <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rassinier" title="Paul Rassinier">Paul Rassinier</a>, whom Barnes called a "distinguished French historian" who had exposed the "exaggerations of the atrocity stories".<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In a 1964 article, "Zionist Fraud", published in the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Mercury" class="mw-redirect" title="American Mercury">American Mercury</a></i>, Barnes wrote: "The courageous author [Rassinier] lays the chief blame for misrepresentation on those whom we must call the swindlers of the crematoria, the Israeli politicians who derive billions of marks from nonexistent, mythical and imaginary cadavers, whose numbers have been reckoned in an unusually distorted and dishonest manner."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Using Rassinier as his source, Barnes claimed that Germany was the victim of aggression in both 1914 and 1939 and that reports of the Holocaust were propaganda to justify a war of aggression against Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_74-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings_of_the_modern_denial_movement">Beginnings of the modern denial movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Beginnings of the modern denial movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KKK_holocaust_a_zionist_hoax.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/KKK_holocaust_a_zionist_hoax.jpg/200px-KKK_holocaust_a_zionist_hoax.jpg" width="200" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f1/KKK_holocaust_a_zionist_hoax.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="381" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KKK_holocaust_a_zionist_hoax.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">KKK</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_salute" title="Nazi salute">Nazi salute</a> and Holocaust denial</div></div></div>
<p>In 1961, a protégé of Barnes, <a href="/wiki/David_Hoggan" class="mw-redirect" title="David Hoggan">David Hoggan</a>, published <i>Der erzwungene Krieg</i> (<i>The Forced War</i>) in West Germany, which claimed that Germany had been the victim of an Anglo-Polish conspiracy in 1939. Though <i>Der erzwungene Krieg</i> was primarily concerned with the origins of World War II, it also down-played or justified the effects of Nazi <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">antisemitic</a> measures in the pre-1939 period.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_71_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_71-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> For example, Hoggan justified the huge one billion <i>Reich</i>-mark fine imposed on the entire Jewish community in Germany after the 1938 <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> as a reasonable measure to prevent what he called "Jewish profiteering" at the expense of German insurance companies and alleged that no Jews were killed in the <i>Kristallnacht</i> (in fact, 91 German Jews were killed in the <i>Kristallnacht</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_71_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipstadt,_Deborah_page_71-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Hoggan explicitly denied the Holocaust in 1969 in a book entitled <i>The Myth of the Six Million</i>, which was published by the <a href="/wiki/Noontide_Press" title="Noontide Press">Noontide Press</a>, a small Los Angeles publisher specializing in antisemitic literature.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1964, Paul Rassinier published <i>The Drama of the European Jews</i>. Rassinier was himself a concentration camp survivor (he was held in <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald" class="mw-redirect" title="Buchenwald">Buchenwald</a> for having helped French Jews escape the Nazis), and modern-day deniers continue to cite his works as scholarly research that questions the accepted facts of the Holocaust. Critics argued that Rassinier did not cite evidence for his claims and ignored information that contradicted his assertions; he nevertheless remains influential in Holocaust denial circles for being one of the first deniers to propose that a vast Zionist/Allied/Soviet conspiracy faked the Holocaust, a theme that would be picked up in later years by other authors.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Austin_App" title="Austin App">Austin App</a>, a <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle University</a> medieval English literature professor, is considered the first major mainstream American holocaust denier.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Atkins,_Stephen_E._2009_pp._153_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atkins,_Stephen_E._2009_pp._153-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> App defended the Germans and Nazi Germany during World War II. He published numerous articles, letters, and books on Holocaust denial, quickly building a loyal following. App's work inspired the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Historical_Review" title="Institute for Historical Review">Institute for Historical Review</a>, a California center founded in 1978 whose sole task is the denial of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The publication of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Butz" title="Arthur Butz">Arthur Butz</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hoax_of_the_Twentieth_Century" title="The Hoax of the Twentieth Century">The Hoax of the Twentieth Century</a>: The case against the presumed extermination of European Jewry</i> in 1976; and <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_War" title="Hitler&#39;s War">Hitler's War</a></i> in 1977 brought other similarly inclined individuals into the fold.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Butz was a tenured associate professor of electrical engineering at <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>. In December 1978 and January 1979, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Faurisson" title="Robert Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>, a French professor of literature at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lyon" title="University of Lyon">University of Lyon</a>, wrote two letters to <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> claiming that the <a href="/wiki/Gas_chambers" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers">gas chambers</a> used by the Nazis to exterminate the Jews did not exist. A colleague of Faurisson, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Pressac" title="Jean-Claude Pressac">Jean-Claude Pressac</a>, who initially shared Faurisson's views, later became convinced of the Holocaust's evidence while investigating documents at <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a> in 1979. He published his conclusions along with much of the underlying evidence in his 1989 book, <i>Auschwitz: Technique and operation of the gas chambers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Bienen" title="Henry Bienen">Henry Bienen</a>, the former president of Northwestern University, has described Arthur Butz's view of the Holocaust as an "embarrassment to Northwestern".<sup id="cite_ref-bienen_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bienen-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, sixty of Butz's colleagues from the Department of Electrical Engineering and Computer Science faculty signed a censure describing Butz's Holocaust denial as "an affront to our humanity and our standards as scholars".<sup id="cite_ref-tdn_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdn-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The letter also called for Butz to "leave our Department and our University and stop trading on our reputation for academic excellence".<sup id="cite_ref-tdn_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdn-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institute_for_Historical_Review">Institute for Historical Review</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Institute for Historical Review">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1978 <a href="/wiki/Willis_Carto" title="Willis Carto">Willis Carto</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Historical_Review" title="Institute for Historical Review">Institute for Historical Review</a> (IHR), an organization dedicated to publicly challenging the commonly accepted history of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-TooCloseForComfort_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TooCloseForComfort-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The IHR's founding was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Austin_App" title="Austin App">Austin App</a>, a <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle</a> professor of medieval English literature and considered the first major American holocaust denier.<sup id="cite_ref-Atkins,_Stephen_E._2009_pp._153_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atkins,_Stephen_E._2009_pp._153-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The IHR sought from the beginning to establish itself within the broad tradition of historical revisionism, by soliciting token supporters who were not from a <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a> background such as <a href="/wiki/James_J._Martin" title="James J. Martin">James J. Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Edward_Konkin_III" title="Samuel Edward Konkin III">Samuel Edward Konkin III</a>, and by promoting the writings of French socialist Paul Rassinier and American anti-war historian Harry Elmer Barnes, in an attempt to show that Holocaust denial had a base of support beyond neo-Nazis. The IHR republished most of Barnes's writings, which had been out of print since his death. While it included articles on other topics and sold books by mainstream historians, the majority of material published and distributed by IHR was devoted to questioning the facts surrounding the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1980, the IHR promised a $50,000 reward to anyone who could prove that Jews were gassed at Auschwitz. <a href="/wiki/Mel_Mermelstein" title="Mel Mermelstein">Mel Mermelstein</a> wrote a <a href="/wiki/Letter_to_the_editor" title="Letter to the editor">letter to the editors</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/LA_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="LA Times">LA Times</a></i> and others including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i>. The IHR wrote back, offering him $50,000 for proof that Jews were, in fact, gassed in the gas chambers at Auschwitz. Mermelstein, in turn, submitted a notarized account of his internment at Auschwitz and how he witnessed Nazi guards ushering his mother and two sisters and others towards (as he learned later) gas chamber number five. Despite this, the IHR refused to pay the reward. Represented by public interest attorney <a href="/wiki/William_John_Cox" title="William John Cox">William John Cox</a>, Mermelstein subsequently sued the IHR in the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Court of Los Angeles County">Superior Court of Los Angeles County</a> for <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract" title="Breach of contract">breach of contract</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anticipatory_repudiation" title="Anticipatory repudiation">anticipatory repudiation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libel" class="mw-redirect" title="Libel">libel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Injurious_denial_of_established_fact&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Injurious denial of established fact (page does not exist)">injurious denial of established fact</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intentional_infliction_of_emotional_distress" title="Intentional infliction of emotional distress">intentional infliction of emotional distress</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Declaratory_relief" class="mw-redirect" title="Declaratory relief">declaratory relief</a> (see <a href="/w/index.php?title=Case_no._C_356_542&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Case no. C 356 542 (page does not exist)">case no. C 356 542</a>). On October 9, 1981, both parties in the Mermelstein case filed motions for <a href="/wiki/Summary_judgment" title="Summary judgment">summary judgment</a> in consideration of which Judge Thomas T. Johnson of the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Court of Los Angeles County">Superior Court of Los Angeles County</a> took "<a href="/wiki/Judicial_notice" title="Judicial notice">judicial notice</a> of the fact that Jews were gassed to death at the Auschwitz Concentration Camp in Poland during the summer of 1944,"<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-order_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-order-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> judicial notice meaning that the court treated the gas chambers as common knowledge, and therefore did not require evidence that the gas chambers existed. On August 5, 1985, Judge Robert A. Wenke entered a judgment based upon the <a href="/wiki/Stipulation" title="Stipulation">Stipulation</a> for Entry of Judgment agreed upon by the parties on July 22, 1985. The judgment required IHR and other defendants to pay $90,000 to Mermelstein and to issue a letter of apology to "Mr. Mel Mermelstein, a survivor of Auschwitz-Birkenau and Buchenwald, and all other survivors of Auschwitz" for "pain, anguish and suffering" caused to them.<sup id="cite_ref-order_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-order-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the "About the IHR" statement on their website, the IHR states, "The IHR does not 'deny' the Holocaust. Indeed, the IHR as such has no 'position' on any specific event...."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Commentators and historians have noted the misleading nature of statements by the IHR that they are not Holocaust deniers. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rauber" title="Paul Rauber">Paul Rauber</a> writes that:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The question [of whether the IHR denies the Holocaust] appears to turn on IHR's Humpty-Dumpty word game with the word Holocaust. According to Mark Weber, associate editor of the IHR's <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Historical_Review" title="Journal of Historical Review">Journal of Historical Review</a> [now Director of the IHR], "If by the 'Holocaust' you mean the political persecution of Jews, some scattered killings, if you mean a cruel thing that happened, no one denies that. But if one says that the 'Holocaust' means the systematic extermination of six to eight million Jews in concentration camps, that's what we think there's not evidence for." That is, IHR doesn't deny that the Holocaust happened; they just deny that the word 'Holocaust' means what people customarily use it for.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>According to British historian of Germany <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Like many individual Holocaust deniers, the Institute as a body denied that it was involved in Holocaust denial. It called this a 'smear' which was 'completely at variance with the facts' because 'revisionist scholars' such as Faurisson, Butz 'and bestselling British historian David Irving acknowledge that hundreds of thousands of Jews were killed and otherwise perished during the Second World War as a direct and indirect result of the harsh anti-Jewish policies of Germany and its allies'. But the concession that a relatively small number of Jews were killed was routinely used by Holocaust deniers to distract attention from the far more important fact of their refusal to admit that the figure ran into the millions, and that a large proportion of these victims were systematically murdered by gassing as well as by shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bradley_Smith_and_the_Committee_for_Open_Debate_on_the_Holocaust">Bradley Smith and the Committee for Open Debate on the Holocaust</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bradley Smith and the Committee for Open Debate on the Holocaust">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1987, Bradley R. Smith, a former media director of the Institute for Historical Review,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> founded the Committee for Open Debate on the Holocaust (CODOH).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, CODOH has repeatedly tried to place advertisements questioning whether the Holocaust happened, especially in college campus newspapers,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> which have not always been rejected as a large number of colleges accepted the ads because they felt not doing so would undercut the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment" class="mw-redirect" title="First Amendment">First Amendment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradley Smith has sought other avenues to promote Holocaust denial&#160;– with little success. On September 8, 2009,  student newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Harvard_Crimson" title="The Harvard Crimson">The Harvard Crimson</a></i> ran a paid ad from Bradley R Smith. It was quickly criticized and an apology was issued from the editor, claiming it was a mistake.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> College newspapers refused Smith's ads from that point until his death in 2016, generally concluding that refusing to accept his paid advertisements did not comprise a violation of Smith's First Amendment rights.
</p><p>Smith referred to his tactics as the CODOH campus project. He said, "I don't want to spend time with adults anymore, I want to go to students. They are superficial. They are empty vessels to be filled." "What I wanted to do was I wanted to set forth three or four ideas that students might be interested in, that might cause them to think about things or to have questions about things. And I wanted to make it as simple as possible, and to set it up in a way that could not really be debated."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust deniers have placed "Full page advertisements in college and university newspapers, including those of <a href="/wiki/Brandeis_University" title="Brandeis University">Brandeis University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Pennsylvania State University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queens_College,_City_University_of_New_York" title="Queens College, City University of New York">Queens College</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">CUNY</a>). Some of these ads arguing that the Holocaust never happened ran without comment; others generated op-ed pieces by professors and students".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="James_Keegstra">James Keegstra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: James Keegstra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/R._v._Keegstra" class="mw-redirect" title="R. v. Keegstra">R. v. Keegstra</a></div>
<p>In 1984, <a href="/wiki/James_Keegstra" title="James Keegstra">James Keegstra</a>, a Canadian high-school teacher, was charged under the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Code_(Canada)" title="Criminal Code (Canada)"><i>Criminal Code</i></a> for "promoting hatred against an identifiable group by communicating anti-Semitic statements to his students".  During class, he would describe Jews as a people of profound evil who had "created the Holocaust to gain sympathy." He also tested his students in exams on his theories and opinion of Jews.
</p><p>Keegstra was charged under s 281.2(2) of the <i>Criminal Code</i> (now s 319(2), which provides that "Every one who, by communicating statements, other than in private conversation, wilfully promotes hatred against any identifiable group" commits a criminal offense.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>  He was convicted at trial before the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Court_of_Queen%27s_Bench" class="mw-redirect" title="Alberta Court of Queen&#39;s Bench">Alberta Court of Queen's Bench</a>.  The court rejected the argument, advanced by Keegstra and his lawyer, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Christie_(lawyer)" title="Doug Christie (lawyer)">Doug Christie</a>, that promoting hatred is a constitutionally protected freedom of expression as per <a href="/wiki/Section_Two_of_the_Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Section Two of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms">s 2(b) of the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms</a>. Keegstra appealed to the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Court_of_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="Alberta Court of Appeal">Alberta Court of Appeal</a>.  That court agreed with Keegstra, and he was acquitted.  The Crown then appealed the case to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>, which ruled by a 4–3 majority that promoting hatred could be <a href="/wiki/R._v._Keegstra#Reasons_of_the_court" class="mw-redirect" title="R. v. Keegstra">justifiably</a> restricted under <a href="/w/index.php?title=Section_1_of_the_Canadian_charter_of_rights_and_freedoms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Section 1 of the Canadian charter of rights and freedoms (page does not exist)">s 1 of the Charter</a>. The Supreme Court restored Keegstra's conviction.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>  He was fired from his teaching position shortly afterward.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Z.C3.BCndel_trials"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Zündel_trials">Zündel trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Zündel trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Leuchter_report" title="Leuchter report">Leuchter report</a></div>
<p>The Toronto-based photo retoucher <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel" title="Ernst Zündel">Ernst Zündel</a> operated a small-press called <a href="/wiki/Samisdat_Publishers" title="Samisdat Publishers">Samisdat Publishers</a>, which published and distributed Holocaust-denial material such as <i><a href="/wiki/Did_Six_Million_Really_Die%3F" title="Did Six Million Really Die?">Did Six Million Really Die?</a></i> by Richard Harwood (a pseudonym of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Verrall_(political_writer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Verrall (political writer)">Richard Verrall</a>&#160;– a British neo-Nazi). In 1985, he was tried in <i><a href="/wiki/R._v._Zundel" class="mw-redirect" title="R. v. Zundel">R. v. Zundel</a></i> and convicted under a "false news" law and sentenced to 15 months imprisonment by an <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> court for "disseminating and publishing material denying the Holocaust".<sup id="cite_ref-Zundelcourt_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zundelcourt-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Holocaust historian <a href="/wiki/Raul_Hilberg" title="Raul Hilberg">Raul Hilberg</a> was a witness for the prosecution at the 1985 trial. Zündel's conviction was overturned in an appeal on a legal technicality, leading to a second trial in 1988, in which he was again convicted. The 1988 trial included, as witnesses for the defense, <a href="/wiki/Fred_A._Leuchter" title="Fred A. Leuchter">Fred A. Leuchter</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Faurisson" title="Robert Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>. The pseudo-scientific <a href="/wiki/Leuchter_report" title="Leuchter report">Leuchter report</a> was presented as a defense document and was published in Canada in 1988 by Zundel's Samisdat Publishers, and in Britain in 1989 by Irving's Focal Point Publishing. In both of his trials, Zündel was defended by <a href="/wiki/Doug_Christie_(lawyer)" title="Doug Christie (lawyer)">Douglas Christie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Kulaszka" title="Barbara Kulaszka">Barbara Kulaszka</a>. His conviction was overturned in 1992 when the Supreme Court of Canada declared the "false news" law unconstitutional.<sup id="cite_ref-Zundelcourt_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zundelcourt-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zündel has a website, web-mastered by his wife Ingrid, which publicises his viewpoints.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In January 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Human_Rights_Commission" title="Canadian Human Rights Commission">Canadian Human Rights Tribunal</a> delivered a ruling in a complaint involving his website, in which it was found to be contravening the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Human_Rights_Act" title="Canadian Human Rights Act">Canadian Human Rights Act</a>. The court ordered Zündel to cease communicating hate messages. In February 2003, the American <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">INS</a> arrested him in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, USA, on an immigration violations matter, and few days later, Zündel was sent back to Canada, where he tried to gain refugee status. Zündel remained in prison until March 1, 2005, when he was deported to Germany and prosecuted for disseminating hate propaganda. On February 15, 2007, Zündel was convicted on 14 counts of incitement under Germany's <i><a href="/wiki/Volksverhetzung" title="Volksverhetzung">Volksverhetzung</a></i> law, which bans the incitement of hatred against a portion of the population, and given the maximum sentence of five years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ernst_Nolte">Ernst Nolte</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ernst Nolte">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The German philosopher and historian <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Nolte" title="Ernst Nolte">Ernst Nolte</a>, starting in the 1980s, advanced a set of theories, which though not denying the Holocaust appeared to flirt with an Italian Holocaust denier, <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Mattogno" title="Carlo Mattogno">Carlo Mattogno</a>,  as a serious historian.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans,_Richard_J._page_83_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans,_Richard_J._page_83-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In a letter to the Israeli historian <a href="/wiki/Otto_Dov_Kulka" title="Otto Dov Kulka">Otto Dov Kulka</a> of December 8, 1986, Nolte criticized the work of the French Holocaust denier <a href="/wiki/Robert_Faurisson" title="Robert Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a> on the ground that the Holocaust did occur, but went on to argue that Faurisson's work was motivated by what Nolte claimed were the admirable motives of sympathy towards the Palestinians and opposition to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In his 1987 book <i>Der europäische Bürgerkrieg</i> (<i>The European Civil War</i>), Nolte claimed that the intentions of Holocaust deniers are "often honourable", and that some of their claims are "not obviously without foundation".<sup id="cite_ref-Evans,_Richard_J._page_83_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans,_Richard_J._page_83-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LipstadtDenying214_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LipstadtDenying214-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Nolte himself, though he has never denied the occurrence of the Holocaust, has claimed that the <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a> of 1942 never happened, and that the minutes of the conference were post-war forgeries done by "biased" Jewish historians designed to discredit Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-LipstadtDenying214_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LipstadtDenying214-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The British historian <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Ian Kershaw</a> has argued that Nolte was operating on the borderlines of Holocaust denial with his implied claim that the "negative myth" of the Third Reich was created by Jewish historians, his allegations of the domination of Holocaust scholarship by "biased" Jewish historians, and his statements that one should withhold judgment on Holocaust deniers, whom Nolte takes considerable pains to stress are not exclusively Germans or fascists.<sup id="cite_ref-Kershaw,_Ian_page_176_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kershaw,_Ian_page_176-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In Kershaw's opinion, Nolte is attempting to imply that perhaps Holocaust deniers are on to something.<sup id="cite_ref-Kershaw,_Ian_page_176_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kershaw,_Ian_page_176-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 1990 interview, Nolte implied that there was something to the <a href="/wiki/Leuchter_report" title="Leuchter report">Leuchter report</a>: "If the revisionists [Holocaust deniers] and Leuchter among them have made it clear to the public that even 'Auschwitz' must be an object of scientific inquiry and controversy then they should be given credit for this. Even if it finally turned out that the number of victims was even greater and the procedures were even more horrific than has been assumed until now."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In his 1993 book <i>Streitpunkte</i> (<i>Points of Contention</i>), Nolte praised the work of Holocaust deniers as superior to "mainstream scholars".<sup id="cite_ref-Wistrich,_Robert_S_pages_293-301_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wistrich,_Robert_S_pages_293-301-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Nolte wrote that "radical revisionists have presented research which, if one is familiar with the source material and the critique of the sources, is probably superior to that of the established historians of Germany".<sup id="cite_ref-Wistrich,_Robert_S_pages_293-301_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wistrich,_Robert_S_pages_293-301-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In a 1994 interview with <i>Der Spiegel</i> magazine, Nolte stated "I cannot rule out the importance of the investigation of the gas chambers in which they looked for remnants of the [chemical process engendered by Zyklon B]", and that "'Of course, I am against revisionists, but Fred Leuchter's 'study' of the Nazi gas ovens has to be given attention, because one has to stay open to 'other' ideas."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
The British historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a> in his 1989 book <i>In Hitler's Shadow</i> expressed the view that Nolte's reputation as a scholar was in ruins as a result of these and other controversial statements on his part.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The American historian <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a> in a 2003 interview stated: </p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Historians such as the German Ernst Nolte are, in some ways, even more dangerous than the deniers. Nolte is an anti-Semite of the first order, who attempts to rehabilitate Hitler by saying that he was no worse than Stalin; but he is careful not to deny the Holocaust. Holocaust-deniers make Nolte's life more comfortable. They have, with their radical argumentation, pulled the center a little more to their side. Consequently, a less radical extremist, such as Nolte, finds himself closer to the middle ground, which makes him more dangerous.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayer_controversy">Mayer controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mayer controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1988, the American historian <a href="/wiki/Arno_J._Mayer" title="Arno J. Mayer">Arno J. Mayer</a> published a book entitled <i>Why Did the Heavens Not Darken?</i>, which did not explicitly deny the Holocaust, but according to <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Dawidowicz" title="Lucy Dawidowicz">Lucy Dawidowicz</a> lent support to Holocaust denial by stating that most people who died at <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a> were the victims of "natural causes" such as disease, not gassing.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Dawidowicz argued that Mayer's statements about Auschwitz were "a breathtaking assertion".<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust historian <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jan_van_Pelt" title="Robert Jan van Pelt">Robert Jan van Pelt</a> has written that Mayer's book is as close as a mainstream historian has ever come to supporting Holocaust denial.<sup id="cite_ref-Pelt_pages_47-48_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pelt_pages_47-48-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust deniers such as <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a> have often cited Mayer's book as one reason for embracing Holocaust denial.<sup id="cite_ref-Pelt_pages_47-48_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pelt_pages_47-48-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Though Mayer has been often condemned for his statement about the reasons for the Auschwitz death toll, his book does not deny the use of gas chambers at Auschwitz, as Holocaust deniers often claim.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some mainstream Holocaust historians have labeled Mayer a denier. The Israeli historian <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> wrote that Mayer "popularizes the nonsense that the Nazis saw in Marxism and Bolshevism their main enemy, and the Jews unfortunately got caught up in this; when he links the destruction of the Jews to the ups and downs of German warfare in the Soviet Union, in a book that is so cocksure of itself that it does not need a proper scientific apparatus, he is really engaging in a much more subtle form of Holocaust denial".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Defenders of Mayer argue that his statement that "Sources for the study of the gas chambers are at once rare and unreliable" has been taken out of context, particularly by Holocaust deniers.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shermer" title="Michael Shermer">Michael Shermer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Grobman" title="Alex Grobman">Alex Grobman</a> observe that the paragraph from which the statement is taken asserts that the SS destroyed the majority of the documentation relating to the operation of the gas chambers in the death camps, which is why Mayer feels that sources for the operation of the gas chambers are "rare" and "unreliable".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ken_McVay_and_alt.revisionism">Ken McVay and <i>alt.revisionism</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ken McVay and alt.revisionism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ken_McVay" class="mw-redirect" title="Ken McVay">Ken McVay</a>, an American resident in Canada, was disturbed by the efforts of organizations like the <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a> to suppress the speech of the Holocaust deniers, feeling that it was better to confront them openly than to try to censor them. On the <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">Usenet</a> newsgroup <i>alt.revisionism</i> he began a campaign of "truth, fact, and evidence", working with other participants on the newsgroup to uncover factual information about the Holocaust and counter the arguments of the deniers by proving them to be based upon misleading evidence, false statements, and outright lies. He founded the <a href="/wiki/Nizkor_Project" title="Nizkor Project">Nizkor Project</a> to expose the activities of the Holocaust deniers, who responded to McVay with personal attacks, slander, and death threats.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="David_Irving_and_the_Lipstadt_libel_case">David Irving and the Lipstadt libel case</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: David Irving and the Lipstadt libel case">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Irving_v_Penguin_Books_and_Lipstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Irving v Penguin Books and Lipstadt">Irving v Penguin Books and Lipstadt</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a>'s 1993 book <i><a href="/wiki/Denying_the_Holocaust" title="Denying the Holocaust">Denying the Holocaust</a></i> sharply criticized various Holocaust deniers, including British author <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a>, for deliberately misrepresenting evidence to justify their preconceived conclusions. In 1996 Irving filed a <a href="/wiki/Libel" class="mw-redirect" title="Libel">libel</a> suit against Lipstadt and her publisher, <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Books" title="Penguin Books">Penguin Books</a>. American historian <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Browning" title="Christopher Browning">Christopher Browning</a>, an expert witness for the defense, wrote a comprehensive essay for the court summarizing the voluminous evidence for the reality of the Holocaust, and under cross-examination, effectively countered all of Irving's principal arguments to the contrary.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a>, another defense expert witness, spent two years examining Irving's writings, and confirmed his misrepresentations, including evidence that he had knowingly used forged documents as source material.
