The judge, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Gray_(judge)" title="Charles Gray (judge)">Justice Charles Gray</a>, ultimately delivered a long and decisive verdict in favor of Lipstadt that referred to Irving as a "Holocaust denier" and "right-wing pro-Nazi <a href="/wiki/Polemic" title="Polemic">polemicist</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Focus_on_Allied_war_crimes_in_Holocaust_denial_literature">Focus on Allied war crimes in Holocaust denial literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Focus on Allied war crimes in Holocaust denial literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The focus on supposed Allied atrocities during the war has been a theme in Holocaust denial literature, particularly in countries where outright denial of the Holocaust is illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> According to historian <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a>, the concept of "comparable Allied wrongs", such as the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Germans_after_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Expulsion of Germans after World War II">expulsion of Germans after World War II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Dresden" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Dresden">bombing of Dresden</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> is at the center of, and a continuously repeated theme of, contemporary <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism_(negationism)#Politically_motivated_historical_revisionism" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical revisionism (negationism)">Holocaust denial</a>; a phenomenon she calls "immoral equivalencies".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Pierre Vidal-Naquet pointed out the same phenomenon in the earlier version of <i>Les Assassins de la mémoire</i> under the title <i>Auschwitz et le tiers monde</i> (<i>Les Assassins de la mémoire</i>, Paris, 2005, pp.&#160;170–180), and accurately about the declarations of <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Barbie" title="Klaus Barbie">Klaus Barbie</a>'s lawyer <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Verg%C3%A8s" title="Jacques Vergès">Jacques Vergès</a>. In 1977, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Broszat" title="Martin Broszat">Martin Broszat</a>, in a review of <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a>'s book <i><a href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_War" title="Hitler&#39;s War">Hitler's War</a></i>, maintained that the picture of World War II drawn by Irving was done in a such way to imply moral equivalence between the actions of the Axis and Allied states with both sides equally guilty of terrible crimes, leading to Hitler's "fanatical, destructive will to annihilate" being downgraded to being "no longer an exceptional phenomenon".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Propaganda">Propaganda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Propaganda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to James Najarian, Holocaust deniers working for the Institute for Historical Review are not trained in history and "put out sham scholarly articles in the mock-academic publication, the <i>Journal of Historical Review</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> They appeal to "our objectivity, our sense of fair play, and our distrust of figurative language".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Thus, they rely on facts to grab the readers' attention. These facts, however, are strung by what Najarian calls "fabricated decorum" and are re-interpreted for their use. For example, they pay particular attention to inconsistencies in numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Holocaust denial propaganda in all forms has been shown to influence the audiences that it reaches. In fact, even the well-educated—that is, college graduates and current university students alike—are susceptible to such propaganda when it is presented before them. This stems from the growing disbelief that audiences feel after being exposed to such information, especially since Holocaust witnesses themselves are decreasing in number.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Studies centered on the psychological effects of Holocaust denial propaganda confirm this assertion. Linda M. Yelland and William F. Stone, in particular, show that Denial essays decrease readers' belief in the Holocaust, regardless of their prior Holocaust awareness.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments">Recent developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Recent developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 1995 the Japanese magazine <i>Marco Polo</i>, a 250,000-circulation monthly published by <a href="/wiki/Bungei_Shunju" class="mw-redirect" title="Bungei Shunju">Bungei Shunju</a>, ran a Holocaust denial article by physician Masanori Nishioka which stated:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The '<a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>' is a fabrication. There were no execution <a href="/wiki/Gas_chambers" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas chambers">gas chambers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a> or in any other <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a>. Today, what are displayed as 'gas chambers' at the remains of the Auschwitz camp in Poland are a post-war fabrication by the Polish communist regime or by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, which controlled the country. Not once, neither at Auschwitz nor in any territory controlled by the Germans during the Second World War, was there 'mass murder of Jews' in 'gas chambers.'<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The Los Angeles-based <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a> instigated a <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> of Bungei Shunju advertisers, including <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cartier_(jeweler)" title="Cartier (jeweler)">Cartier</a>. Within days, Bungei Shunju shut down <i>Marco Polo</i> and its editor, Kazuyoshi Hanada, quit, as did the president of Bungei Shunju, Kengo Tanaka.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Turkey, in 1996, the Islamic preacher <a href="/wiki/Harun_Yahya" class="mw-redirect" title="Harun Yahya">Harun Yahya</a> distributed thousands of copies of a book which was originally published the previous year, entitled <i>Soykırım Yalanı</i> ("The Holocaust Lie") and mailed unsolicited texts to American and European schools and colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The publication of <i>Soykırım Yalanı</i> sparked much public debate.<sup id="cite_ref-axt_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axt-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> This book claims, "what is presented as Holocaust is the death of some Jews due to the typhus plague during the war and the famine towards the end of the war caused by the defeat of the Germans."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In March 1996, a Turkish painter and intellectual, <a href="/wiki/Bedri_Baykam" title="Bedri Baykam">Bedri Baykam</a>, published a strongly worded critique of the book in the Ankara daily newspaper <i>Siyah-Beyaz</i> ("Black and White"). A legal suit for slander was brought against him. During the trial in September, Baykam exposed the real author of the book as <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Oktar" title="Adnan Oktar">Adnan Oktar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-axt_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axt-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The suit was withdrawn in March 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In France, Holocaust denial became more prominent in the 1990s as <i><a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism_(negationism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical revisionism (negationism)">négationnisme</a></i>, though the movement has existed in ultra-left French politics since at least the 1960s, led by figures such as <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Guillaume" title="Pierre Guillaume">Pierre Guillaume</a> (who was involved in the bookshop <a href="/wiki/La_Vieille_Taupe" title="La Vieille Taupe">La Vieille Taupe</a> during the 1960s). Recently, elements of the extreme far right in France have begun to build on each other's negationist arguments, which often span beyond the Holocaust to cover a range of antisemitic views, incorporating attempts to tie the Holocaust to the Biblical massacre of the <a href="/wiki/Canaanites" class="mw-redirect" title="Canaanites">Canaanites</a>, critiques of Zionism, and other material fanning what has been called a "conspiratorial Judeo-phobia" designed to legitimize and "banalize" antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Belgium in 2001, <a href="/wiki/Roeland_Raes" title="Roeland Raes">Roeland Raes</a>, the ideologue and vice-president of one of the country's largest political parties, the <a href="/wiki/Vlaams_Belang" title="Vlaams Belang">Vlaams Belang</a> (formerly named <a href="/wiki/Vlaams_Blok" title="Vlaams Blok">Vlaams Blok</a>, Flemish Bloc), gave an interview on Dutch TV where he cast doubt over the number of Jews murdered by the Nazis during the Holocaust. In the same interview he questioned the scale of the Nazis' use of gas chambers and the authenticity of <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a>'s diary. In response to the media assault following the interview, Raes was forced to resign his position but vowed to remain active within the party.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Three years later, the Vlaams Blok was convicted of racism and chose to disband. Immediately afterwards, it legally reformed under the new name Vlaams Belang (Flemish Interest) with the same leaders and the same membership.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The trial of a Canadian woman, Monika Schaefer and her German-Canadian brother, Alfred Schaefer started in Germany in early July 2018. They were charged with <i>Volksverhetzung</i>, "incitement to hatred". The pair had published video clips on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> of their denial of the genocide of Jews. In the clips, Alfred Schaefer said that Jews wanted to destroy Germans, blamed them for starting both World Wars, and referred to the Holocaust as a "Jewish fantasy".<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Monika Schaefer was arrested in January 2018 in Germany while attending a court hearing of <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Stolz" title="Sylvia Stolz">Sylvia Stolz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Schaefer had been the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Canada" title="Green Party of Canada">Green Party</a> candidate in the <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> riding of <a href="/wiki/Yellowhead_(electoral_district)" title="Yellowhead (electoral district)">Yellowhead</a> during the federal elections in 2006, 2008, and 2011, but was expelled from the party after news reports surfaced of a July 2016 video<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> where she describes the Holocaust as "the most persistent lie in all of history" and insisted that those in concentration camps had been kept as healthy and as well-fed as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Denials of the Holocaust have been promoted by various Middle Eastern figures and media. Holocaust denial is sponsored by some Middle Eastern governments, including Iran<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> and Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-JVL-SYR_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JVL-SYR-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Prominent figures from the Middle East have rarely made publicized visits to <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>—<a href="/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel" title="Arab citizens of Israel">Israel's Arab community</a> being the exception. In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Hadash" title="Hadash">Hadash</a> MK <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Barakeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed Barakeh">Mohammed Barakeh</a> visited, following a previous visit of two other Arab-Israeli lawmakers, and a group of about 100 Arab-Israeli writers and clerics in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-MK_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MK-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Individuals from the <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syrian</a> government, the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>, and a number of Palestinian groups have all engaged in various aspects of Holocaust denial.<sup id="cite_ref-JVL-SYR_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JVL-SYR-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Karsh98_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh98-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 2006 <a href="/wiki/Robert_Satloff" title="Robert Satloff">Robert Satloff</a> writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, reported that "A respected Holocaust research institution recently reported that Egypt, Qatar and Saudi Arabia all promote Holocaust denial and protect Holocaust deniers."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> leaders have promoted Holocaust denial; <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Aziz_al-Rantissi" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdel Aziz al-Rantissi">Abdel Aziz al-Rantissi</a> held that the Holocaust never occurred, that <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionists</a> were behind the action of Nazis, and that Zionists funded Nazism.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (April 2018)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A press release by Hamas in April 2000 decried "the so-called Holocaust, which is an alleged and invented story with no basis".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In August 2009, Hamas' <a href="/wiki/Hamas%E2%80%93UNRWA_Holocaust_dispute" title="Hamas–UNRWA Holocaust dispute">told UNRWA</a> that it would "refuse" to allow Palestinian children to study the Holocaust, which it called "a lie invented by the Zionists" and referred to Holocaust education as a "war crime".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Hamas continued to hold this position in 2011, when the organization's Ministry for Refugee Affairs said that Holocaust education was "intended to poison the minds of our children."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>, the President of Egypt, told a German newspaper in 1964 that "no person, not even the most simple one, takes seriously the lie of the six million Jews that were murdered [in the Holocaust]."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The thesis of the 1982 doctoral dissertation of <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, a co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> and president of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a>, was "The Secret Connection between the Nazis and the Leaders of the Zionist Movement".<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wiesenthal_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiesenthal-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In his 1983 book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Side:_the_Secret_Relationship_Between_Nazism_and_Zionism" class="mw-redirect" title="The Other Side: the Secret Relationship Between Nazism and Zionism">The Other Side: the Secret Relationship Between Nazism and Zionism</a></i> based on the dissertation, Abbas denied that six million Jews had died in the Holocaust; dismissing it as a "myth" and a "fantastic lie".<sup id="cite_ref-Abbas_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbas-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> At most, he wrote, 890,000 Jews were killed by the Germans. Abbas claimed that the number of deaths has been exaggerated for political purposes. "It seems that the interest of the Zionist movement, however, is to inflate this figure [of Holocaust deaths] so that their gains will be greater. This led them to emphasize this figure [six million] in order to gain the solidarity of international public opinion with Zionism. Many scholars have debated the figure of six million and reached stunning conclusions—fixing the number of Jewish victims at only a few hundred thousand."<sup id="cite_ref-wiesenthal_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiesenthal-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wymaninstitute.org_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wymaninstitute.org-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In his March 2006 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i>, Abbas stated, "I wrote in detail about the Holocaust and said I did not want to discuss numbers. I quoted an argument between historians in which various numbers of casualties were mentioned. One wrote there were 12&#160;million victims and another wrote there were 800,000. I have no desire to argue with the figures. The Holocaust was a terrible, unforgivable crime against the Jewish nation, a crime against humanity that cannot be accepted by humankind. The Holocaust was a terrible thing and nobody can claim I denied it."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> While acknowledging the existence of the Holocaust in 2006 and 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-Heinous_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinous-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Abbas has defended the position that Zionists collaborated with the Nazis to perpetrate it. In 2012, Abbas told <a href="/wiki/Al_Mayadeen" title="Al Mayadeen">Al Mayadeen</a>, a Beirut TV station affiliated with Iran and Hezbollah, that he "challenges anyone who can deny that the Zionist movement had ties with the Nazis before World War II".<sup id="cite_ref-Link_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Link-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Surveys conducted by <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Smooha" title="Sammy Smooha">Sammy Smooha</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Haifa" title="University of Haifa">University of Haifa</a> found that the fraction of Israeli Arabs denying that millions of Jews were murdered by the Nazis increased from 28% in 2006 to 40% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Smooha_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smooha-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Smooha commented:
</p>
<blockquote><p>In Arab eyes disbelief in the very happening of the Shoah is not hate of Jews (embedded in the denial of the Shoah in the West) but rather a form of protest. Arabs not believing in the event of Shoah intend to express strong objection to the portrayal of the Jews as the ultimate victim and to the underrating of the Palestinians as a victim. They deny Israel's right to exist as a Jewish state that the Shoah gives legitimacy to. Arab disbelief in the Shoah is a component of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, unlike the ideological and anti-Semitic denial of the Holocaust and the desire to escape guilt in the West.<sup id="cite_ref-Smooha_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smooha-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Former Iranian President <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a> frequently denied the Holocaust,<sup id="cite_ref-InternationalList1_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InternationalList1-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> formally 'questioning' the reliability of the historical evidence,<sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> although he on occasion confirmed belief in it.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> In a December 2005 speech, Ahmadinejad said that a legend was fabricated and had been promoted to protect <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. He said:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>They have fabricated a legend, under the name of the Massacre of the Jews, and they hold it higher than God himself, religion itself and the prophets themselves.... If somebody in their country questions God, nobody says anything, but if somebody denies the myth of the massacre of Jews, the Zionist loudspeakers and the governments in the pay of Zionism will start to scream.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The remarks immediately provoked international controversy as well as swift condemnation from government officials in Israel, Europe, and the United States. All six political parties in the German parliament signed a joint resolution condemning this Holocaust denial.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> political leader <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Mashaal" class="mw-redirect" title="Khaled Mashaal">Khaled Mashaal</a> described Ahmadinejad's comments as "courageous" and stated, "Muslim people will defend Iran because it voices what they have in their hearts, in particular the Palestinian people."<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Public_Affairs_Council" title="Muslim Public Affairs Council">Muslim Public Affairs Council</a> condemned Ahmadinejad's remarks.<sup id="cite_ref-mpac_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mpac-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 the Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a> leader, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Mahdi_Akef" title="Mohammed Mahdi Akef">Mohammed Mahdi Akef</a>, denounced what he called "the myth of the Holocaust" in defending Ahmadinejad's denial of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 11, 2006, the Iranian state-sponsored "<a href="/wiki/International_Conference_to_Review_the_Global_Vision_of_the_Holocaust" title="International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust">International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust</a>" opened to widespread condemnation.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The conference, called for by and held at the behest of Ahmadinejad,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> was widely described as a "Holocaust denial conference" or a "meeting of Holocaust deniers",<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> though Iran denied it was a Holocaust denial conference.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> A few months before it opened, the Iranian Foreign Ministry spokesman Hamid Reza Asefi stated: "The Holocaust is not a sacred issue that one can't touch. I have visited the Nazi camps in Eastern Europe. I think it is exaggerated."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, in an interview with CNN, newly elected Iranian President <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani" title="Hassan Rouhani">Hassan Rouhani</a> was quoted as condemning the Holocaust, stating, "I can tell you that any crime that happens in history against humanity, including the crime the Nazis created towards the Jews as well as non-Jews is reprehensible and condemnable. Whatever criminality they committed against the Jews, we condemn."<sup id="cite_ref-Saeed_Kamali_Dehghan_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saeed_Kamali_Dehghan-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>  Iranian media later accused CNN of fabricating Rouhani's comments.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his official 2013 <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a> address, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran" title="Supreme Leader of Iran">Supreme Leader of Iran</a> <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ayatollah_Ali_Khamenei" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Ayatollah Ali Khamenei">Grand Ayatollah Ali Khamenei</a> questioned the veracity of the Holocaust, remarking that "The Holocaust is an event whose reality is uncertain and if it has happened, it's uncertain how it has happened."<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> This was consistent with Khamenei's previous comments regarding the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, the House of Cartoon and the Sarcheshmeh Cultural Complex in Iran organized the <a href="/wiki/International_Holocaust_Cartoon_Competition" title="International Holocaust Cartoon Competition">International Holocaust Cartoon Competition</a>, a competition in which artists were encouraged to submit <a href="/wiki/Cartoons" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartoons">cartoons</a> on the theme of Holocaust denial. The winner of the contest will receive $12,000.  <i><a href="/wiki/Hamshahri" title="Hamshahri">Hamshahri</a></i>, a popular Iranian newspaper, held a <a href="/wiki/International_Holocaust_Cartoon_Competition" title="International Holocaust Cartoon Competition">similar contest</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_Holocaust_denial">Reactions to Holocaust denial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Reactions to Holocaust denial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Holocaust_denial" title="Criticism of Holocaust denial">Criticism of Holocaust denial</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_reaction">Types of reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Types of reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Scholarly response to Holocaust denial can be roughly divided into three categories. Some academics refuse to engage Holocaust deniers or their arguments at all, on grounds that doing so lends them unwarranted legitimacy.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> A second group of scholars, typified by the American historian <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a>, have tried to raise awareness of the methods and motivations of Holocaust denial without legitimizing the deniers themselves. "We need not waste time or effort answering the deniers' contentions," Lipstadt wrote. "It would be never-ending.... Their commitment is to an ideology and their 'findings' are shaped to support it."<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> A third group, typified by the <a href="/wiki/Nizkor_Project" title="Nizkor Project">Nizkor Project</a>, responds to arguments and claims made by Holocaust denial groups by pointing out inaccuracies and errors in their evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-66-q&amp;a_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66-q&amp;a-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Even scholarly responses, however, can trigger vigorous rebuttals. In 1996, the British Holocaust denier <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a> brought <a href="/wiki/Irving_v_Penguin_Books_and_Lipstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Irving v Penguin Books and Lipstadt">a civil defamation suit</a> against Lipstadt and her publisher, stemming from Lipstadt's book <i><a href="/wiki/Denying_the_Holocaust" title="Denying the Holocaust">Denying the Holocaust</a></i>, in which she named Irving as "one of the more dangerous" Holocaust deniers, because he was a published author, and was viewed by some as a legitimate military historian. He was "familiar with historical evidence", she wrote, and "bends it until it conforms with his ideological leanings and political agenda". Irving, who appeared as a defense witness in <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Z%C3%BCndel" title="Ernst Zündel">Ernst Zündel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/R._v._Zundel" class="mw-redirect" title="R. v. Zundel">trial</a> in Canada, and once declared at a rally of Holocaust deniers that "more women died in the <a href="/wiki/Chappaquiddick_incident" title="Chappaquiddick incident">back seat of Edward Kennedy's car</a> than ever died in a gas chamber at <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> claimed that Lipstadt's allegation damaged his reputation. After a two-month trial in London, the trial judge issued a 333-page ruling against Irving.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1991 the <a href="/wiki/American_Historical_Association" title="American Historical Association">American Historical Association</a> issued the following statement: <i>The American Historical Association Council strongly deplores the publicly reported attempts to deny the fact of the Holocaust. No serious historian questions that the Holocaust took place.</i> This followed a strong reaction by many of its members and commentary in the press against a near-unanimous decision that the AHA had made in May 1991 that studying the <i>significance of the Holocaust</i> should be encouraged. The association's May 1991 statement was in response to an incident where certain of its members had questioned the reality of the Holocaust. The December 1991 declaration is a reversal of the AHA's earlier stance that the association should not set a precedent by certifying historical facts.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_figures_and_scholars">Public figures and scholars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Public figures and scholars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of public figures and scholars have spoken out against Holocaust denial, with some – such as literary theorist <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baudrillard" title="Jean Baudrillard">Jean Baudrillard</a> – likening Holocaust denial to "part of the extermination itself".<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Historical_Association" title="American Historical Association">American Historical Association</a>, the oldest and largest society of historians and teachers of history in the United States, states that Holocaust denial is "at best, a form of academic fraud".<sup id="cite_ref-adaaha_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adaaha-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, UN Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> said: "Remembering is a necessary rebuke to those who say the Holocaust never happened or has been exaggerated. Holocaust denial is the work of bigots; we must reject their false claims whenever, wherever and by whomever they are made."<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Holocaust survivor and Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Elie_Wiesel" title="Elie Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>, during a 1999 discussion at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in Washington D.C., called the Holocaust "the most documented tragedy in <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>. Never before has a tragedy elicited so much witness from the killers, from the victims and even from the bystanders—millions of pieces here in the museum what you have, all other museums, archives in the thousands, in the millions."<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2007, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> condemned "without reservation any denial of the Holocaust", though Iran disassociated itself from the resolution.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In July 2013, Iran's then president-elect Hassan Rohani described Ahmadinejad's remarks about the Holocaust and Israel as "<a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">hate</a> rhetoric"<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and in September 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani" title="Hassan Rouhani">Rohani</a> stated that "The Nazis carried out a massacre that cannot be denied, especially against the Jewish people" and "The massacre by the Nazis was condemnable. We never want to sit by side with the Nazis..They committed a crime against Jews — which is a crime against..all of humanity."<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> While declining to give a specific number of Jewish victims, Iranian analysts suggested that "Rouhani pushed the envelope as far as it could go..without infuriating the supreme leader, Ayatollah Ali Khamenei, and other conservatives back home."<sup id="cite_ref-Saeed_Kamali_Dehghan_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saeed_Kamali_Dehghan-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_SS_members">Former SS members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Former SS members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Critics of Holocaust denial also include members of the Auschwitz SS. Camp physician and SS-<i><a href="/wiki/Untersturmf%C3%BChrer" title="Untersturmführer">Untersturmführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hans_M%C3%BCnch" title="Hans Münch">Hans Münch</a> considered the facts of Auschwitz "so firmly determined that one cannot have any doubt at all", and described those who negate what happened at the camp as "malevolent" people who have "personal interest to want to bury in silence things that cannot be buried in silence".<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zyklon_B" title="Zyklon B">Zyklon B</a> handler and SS-<i><a href="/wiki/Oberscharf%C3%BChrer" title="Oberscharführer">Oberscharführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Josef_Klehr" title="Josef Klehr">Josef Klehr</a> said that anyone who maintains that nobody was gassed at Auschwitz must be "crazy or in the wrong".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> SS-<i>Unterscharführer</i> <a href="/wiki/Oswald_Kaduk" title="Oswald Kaduk">Oswald Kaduk</a> stated that he did not consider those who maintain such a thing as normal people.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Hearing about Holocaust denial compelled former SS-<i><a href="/wiki/Rottenf%C3%BChrer" title="Rottenführer">Rottenführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Gr%C3%B6ning" title="Oskar Gröning">Oskar Gröning</a> to publicly speak about what he witnessed at Auschwitz, and denounce Holocaust deniers,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> stating:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I would like you to believe me. I saw the gas chambers. I saw the crematoria. I saw the open fires. I was on the ramp when the selections took place. I would like you to believe that these atrocities happened because I was there.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Online_2005_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Online_2005-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holocaust_denial_and_antisemitism">Holocaust denial and antisemitism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Holocaust denial and antisemitism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Encyclopedia of Genocide and Crimes Against Humanity</i> defines Holocaust denial as "a new form of anti-Semitism, but one that hinges on age-old motifs".<sup id="cite_ref-EGCAH45_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EGCAH45-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> has stated that "Holocaust denial is a contemporary form of the classic anti-Semitic doctrine of the evil, manipulative and threatening world Jewish conspiracy"<sup id="cite_ref-ADLguide_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADLguide-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and French historian Valérie Igounet has written that "Holocaust denial is a convenient polemical substitute for anti-semitism."<sup id="cite_ref-Igounet_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Igounet-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Walter Reich, psychiatrist and then senior scholar at the <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson_International_Center_for_Scholars" title="Woodrow Wilson International Center for Scholars">Woodrow Wilson International Center for Scholars</a>, one-time director of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum">United States Holocaust Memorial Museum</a>, and now professor of international affairs at <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University" title="George Washington University">George Washington University</a>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The primary motivation for most deniers is anti-Semitism, and for them the Holocaust is an infuriatingly inconvenient fact of history. After all, the Holocaust has generally been recognized as one of the most terrible crimes that ever took place, and surely the very emblem of evil in the modern age. If that crime was a direct result of anti-Semitism taken to its logical end, then anti-Semitism itself, even when expressed in private conversation, is inevitably discredited among most people. What better way to rehabilitate anti-Semitism, make anti-Semitic arguments seem once again respectable in civilized discourse and even make it acceptable for governments to pursue anti-Semitic policies than by convincing the world that the great crime for which anti-Semitism was blamed simply never happened—indeed, that it was nothing more than a frame-up invented by the Jews, and propagated by them through their control of the media? What better way, in short, to make the world safe again for anti-Semitism than by denying the Holocaust?<sup id="cite_ref-ReichNYT_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReichNYT-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The French historian <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Vidal-Naquet" title="Pierre Vidal-Naquet">Pierre Vidal-Naquet</a> described the motivation of deniers more succinctly:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>One revives the dead in order the better to strike the living.<sup id="cite_ref-Vidal-NaquetMotivations_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vidal-NaquetMotivations-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_of_antisemitism">Definition of antisemitism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Definition of antisemitism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Working_Definition_of_Antisemitism" title="Working Definition of Antisemitism">Working Definition of Antisemitism</a></div>
<p>In 2005, the European Monitoring Centre on Racism and Xenophobia (EUMC) published a working definition of antisemitism which gave as an example of the way that antisemitism might manifest itself.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Denying the fact, scope, mechanisms (e.g., gas chambers) or intentionality of the genocide of the Jewish people at the hands of National Socialist Germany and its supporters and accomplices during World War II (the Holocaust).<sup id="cite_ref-EFRAWorkingDefinition_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFRAWorkingDefinition-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> 
</p></blockquote>
<p>A definition based on the EUMC definition was later adopted by the U.S. Department of State.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Accusing the Jews as a people, or Israel as a state, of inventing or exaggerating the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In November 2013 the Fundamental Rights Agency (FRA) the successor agency to the EUMC removed the definition from the organisation's website in 'a clear-out of non-official documents'. A spokesperson stated that the document had never been viewed as a valid definition and that "We are not aware of any official definition".<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ToI_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToI-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> On 26 May 2016 the International Holocaust Remembrance Alliance adopted a working definition of  antisemitism and called on the EU to adopt this definition. The United Kingdom was the first country to adopted the definition followed by Israel, Austria,  Scotland,  Romania, Germany and Bulgaria. The European Parliament voted in favor of a resolution calling for member states to adopt the definition on 1 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The definition includes as one example of contemporary antisemitism the following.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Denying the fact, scope, mechanisms (e.g. gas chambers) or intentionality of the genocide of the Jewish people at the hands of National Socialist Germany and its supporters and accomplices during World War II (the Holocaust).<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examination_of_claims">Examination of claims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Examination of claims">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Holocaust_denial" title="Criticism of Holocaust denial">Criticism of Holocaust denial</a></div>
<p>The key claims which cause Holocaust denial to differ from established fact are:<sup id="cite_ref-Key_elements_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Key_elements-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The Nazis had no official policy or intention of exterminating Jews.</li>
<li>Nazis did not use <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber" title="Gas chamber">gas chambers</a> to mass murder Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-NP-gas-chambers_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NP-gas-chambers-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The figure of 5 to 6&#160;million Jewish deaths is a gross exaggeration, and the actual number is an <a href="/wiki/Order_of_magnitude" title="Order of magnitude">order of magnitude</a> lower.</li></ul>
<p>Other claims include the following:
</p>
<ul><li>Stories of the Holocaust were a myth initially created by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies of World War II</a> to demonize Germans,<sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Jews having spread this myth as part of a grander plot intended to enable the creation of a Jewish homeland in <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, and now to garner continuing support for the state of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Documentary evidence of the Holocaust, from photographs to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diary_of_a_Young_Girl" title="The Diary of a Young Girl">The Diary of Anne Frank</a></i>, is fabricated.<sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Survivor testimonies are filled with errors and inconsistencies, and are thus unreliable.<sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Interrogators obtained Nazi prisoners' confessions of war crimes through the use of torture.<sup id="cite_ref-Assertions_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assertions-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Nazi treatment of Jews was no different from what the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> did to their enemies in World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Holocaust denial is widely viewed as failing to adhere to <a href="/wiki/Historical_method" title="Historical method">principles for the treatment of evidence</a> that mainstream historians (as well as scholars in other fields) regard as basic to <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">rational inquiry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Holocaust was well documented by the <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a> of the Nazi government itself.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> It was further witnessed by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> forces who entered Germany and its associated <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> states towards the end of World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>  It was also witnessed from the inside by non-Jewish captives such as Catholic <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance">French Resistance</a> member <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rogerie" title="André Rogerie">André Rogerie</a> who wrote extensively and testified about his experiences in seven camps including Auschwitz-Birkenau<sup id="cite_ref-ina-shoah_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ina-shoah-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> and also produced the oldest contemporary sketch of a camp crematorium.<sup id="cite_ref-Wieviorka_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wieviorka-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to researchers <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shermer" title="Michael Shermer">Michael Shermer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Grobman" title="Alex Grobman">Alex Grobman</a>, there is a "convergence of evidence" that proves that the Holocaust happened. This evidence includes:<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jew_demogr.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jew_demogr.png/300px-Jew_demogr.png" width="300" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jew_demogr.png/450px-Jew_demogr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jew_demogr.png/600px-Jew_demogr.png 2x" data-file-width="733" data-file-height="483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jew_demogr.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jewish World Population without Holocaust (mln people) by <a href="/wiki/Sergio_DellaPergola" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergio DellaPergola">Sergio DellaPergola</a></div></div></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote">
<ol><li><i>Written documents</i>—hundreds of thousands of letters, memos, blueprints, orders, bills, speeches, articles, memoirs, and confessions.</li>
<li><i>Eyewitness testimony</i>—accounts from survivors, Jewish <a href="/wiki/Sonderkommando" title="Sonderkommando">Sonderkommandos</a> (who helped load bodies from the gas chambers into the crematoria in exchange for a chance of survival), <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> guards, commandants, local townspeople, and even high-ranking Nazis who spoke openly about the mass murder of the Jews.</li>
<li><i>Photographs</i>—including official military and press photographs, civilian photographs, secret photographs taken by survivors, aerial photographs, German and Allied film footage, and unofficial photographs taken by the German military.</li>
<li><i>The camps themselves</i>—concentration camps, work camps, and <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a> that still exist in varying degrees of originality and reconstruction.</li>
<li><i>Inferential evidence</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Argument_from_silence" title="Argument from silence">argument from silence</a></i> — population demographics, reconstructed from the pre–World War II era; if six million Jews were not killed, what happened to them?</li></ol>
</blockquote>
<p>Much of the controversy surrounding the claims of Holocaust deniers centers on the methods used to present arguments that the Holocaust allegedly <i>never happened as commonly accepted</i>. Numerous accounts have been given by Holocaust deniers (including evidence presented in court cases) of claimed facts and evidence; however, independent research has shown these claims to be based upon flawed research, biased statements, or even deliberately falsified evidence. Opponents of Holocaust denial have documented numerous instances in which such evidence was altered or manufactured (see <a href="/wiki/Nizkor_Project" title="Nizkor Project">Nizkor Project</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Irving" title="David Irving">David Irving</a>). According to <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Vidal-Naquet" title="Pierre Vidal-Naquet">Pierre Vidal-Naquet</a>, "in our society of image and spectacle, extermination on paper leads to extermination in reality."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws_against_Holocaust_denial">Laws against Holocaust denial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Laws against Holocaust denial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial" title="Laws against Holocaust denial">Laws against Holocaust denial</a></div>
<p>Holocaust denial is explicitly or implicitly illegal in 17 countries: <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Romania officially denied the Holocaust occurred on its territory up until the <a href="/wiki/Wiesel_Commission" title="Wiesel Commission">Wiesel Commission</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-news_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-news-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> The European Union's Framework decision on Racism and Xenophobia states that denying or grossly trivializing "crimes of genocide" should be made "punishable in all <a href="/wiki/EU_Member_States" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Member States">EU Member States</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Slovakia criminalized denial of fascist crimes in general in late 2001; in May 2005, the term "Holocaust" was explicitly adopted by the penal code and in 2009, it became illegal to deny any act regarded by an international criminal court as genocide. In 2010 the Parliament of Hungary adopted legislation punishing the denial of the genocides committed by National Socialist or Communist systems, without mentioning the word "Holocaust".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Such legislation remains controversial. In October 2007, a tribunal declared Spain's Holocaust denial law <a href="/wiki/Unconstitutional" class="mw-redirect" title="Unconstitutional">unconstitutional</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Italy rejected a denial law proposing a prison sentence of up to four years. In 2006 the Netherlands rejected a draft law proposing a maximum sentence of one year on denial of genocidal acts in general, although specifically denying the Holocaust remains a criminal offense there. The United Kingdom has twice rejected <a href="/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial" title="Laws against Holocaust denial">Holocaust denial laws</a>. Denmark and Sweden have also rejected such legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of deniers have been prosecuted under various countries' denial laws. French literature professor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Faurisson" title="Robert Faurisson">Robert Faurisson</a>, for example, was convicted and punished under the <a href="/wiki/Gayssot_Act" title="Gayssot Act">Gayssot Act</a> in 1990. Some historians oppose such laws, among them <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Vidal-Naquet" title="Pierre Vidal-Naquet">Pierre Vidal-Naquet</a>, an outspoken critic of Faurisson, on the grounds that denial legislation imposes "historical truth as legal truth".<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Other academics favor <a href="/wiki/Criminalization" title="Criminalization">criminalization</a>. Holocaust denial, they contend, is "the worst form of racism and its most respectable version because it pretends to be a research".<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="David_Irving_conviction">David Irving conviction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: David Irving conviction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2006 Irving was convicted in Austria, where Holocaust denial is illegal, for a speech he had made in 1989 in which he denied the existence of gas chambers at Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-release_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Irving was aware of the outstanding arrest warrant, but chose to go to Austria anyway "to give a lecture to a far-right student fraternity".<sup id="cite_ref-release_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Although he pleaded guilty to the charge, Irving said he had been "mistaken", and had changed his opinions on the Holocaust. "I said that then, based on my knowledge at the time, but by 1991 when I came across the Eichmann papers, I wasn't saying that anymore and I wouldn't say that now. The Nazis did murder millions of Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCCenshorship_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCenshorship-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Irving served 13 months of a 3-year sentence in an Austrian prison, including the period between his arrest and conviction, and was deported in early 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-release_226-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The episode sparked intense international debate over the limits of freedom of speech. Upon hearing of Irving's sentence, Lipstadt said, "I am not happy when censorship wins, and I don't believe in winning battles via censorship.... The way of fighting Holocaust deniers is with history and with truth."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCCenshorship_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCenshorship-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a></i>, upon Irving's return to the UK, he "vow[ed] to repeat views denying the Holocaust that led to his conviction" stating he felt "no need any longer to show remorse" for his Holocaust views.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genocide_denials">Genocide denials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Genocide denials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Genocide_denial" title="Genocide denial">Genocide denial</a></div>
<p>Other acts of genocide have met similar attempts to deny and minimize them. <a href="/wiki/Gregory_H._Stanton" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregory H. Stanton">Gregory H. Stanton</a>, formerly of the US State Department and the founder of Genocide Watch, lists denial as the final stage of a genocide development: "Denial is the eighth stage that always follows a genocide. It is among the surest indicators of further <a href="/wiki/Genocidal_massacre" title="Genocidal massacre">genocidal massacres</a>. The perpetrators of genocide dig up the mass graves, burn the bodies, try to cover up the evidence and intimidate the witnesses. They deny that they committed any crimes, and often blame what happened on the victims."<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Holocaust_deniers">Notable Holocaust deniers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocaust_denial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notable Holocaust deniers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
